2983 <section id="_53">

2984

2985 <h2>

2986Treatment of Newly Diagnosed AML</h2>

2987

2988 <div id="_section_53" class="pdq-sections">

2989<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

2990<h6>

2991In This Section</h6>

2992<ul>

2993<li>

2994<a href="#_628_toc">

2995Treatment Options for Newly Diagnosed (Untreated; Remission Induction) AML<ul>

2996<li>

2997<a href="#_550_toc">

2998Chemotherapy</a>

2999</li>

3000</ul>

3001</a>

3002</li>

3003<li>

3004<a href="#_TrialSearch_53_sid_4_toc">

3005Current Clinical Trials</a>

3006</li>

3007</ul>

3008</nav>

3009<section id="_628">

3010<h3 id="_628_toc">

3011Treatment Options for Newly Diagnosed (Untreated; Remission Induction) AML</h3>

3012<p id="_629" tabindex="-1">

3013Treatment options for newly diagnosed (untreated; remission induction) acute myeloid leukemia (AML) include the following:</p>

3014<div class="pdq-content-list">

3015<ol id="_630">

3016<li>

3017<a href="/types/leukemia/hp/adult-aml-treatment-pdq#_550">

3018Chemotherapy</a>

3019.</li>

3020</ol>

3021</div>

3022<section id="_550">

3023<h4 id="_550_toc">

3024Chemotherapy</h4>

3025<p id="_607" tabindex="-1">

3026Chemotherapy for AML is divided into the following two general categories:</p>

3027<div class="pdq-content-list">

3028<ol id="_608">

3029<li>

3030 Intensive remission-induction chemotherapy. </li>

3031<li>

3032 Nonintensive chemotherapy. </li>

3033</ol>

3034</div>

3035<p id="_510" tabindex="-1">

3036One of the following combination chemotherapy regimens may be used as intensive remission induction therapy:</p>

3037<div class="pdq-content-list">

3038<ul id="_401">

3039<li>

3040Cytarabine plus daunorubicin.[<a href="#cit/section_4.1">

30411</a>

3042,<a href="#cit/section_4.2">

30432</a>

3044]

3045</li>

3046<li>

3047Cytarabine plus idarubicin.[<a href="#cit/section_4.3">

30483</a>

3049-<a href="#cit/section_4.6">

30506</a>

3051]

3052</li>

3053<li>

3054Cytarabine plus mitoxantrone.[<a href="#cit/section_4.7">

30557</a>

3056]</li>

3057<li>

3058Cytarabine plus anthracycline plus midostaurin.[<a href="#cit/section_4.8">

30598</a>

3060] </li>

3061<li>

3062 Cytarabine plus anthracycline plus gemtuzumab ozogamicin.[<a href="#cit/section_4.9">

30639</a>

3064] </li>

3065<li>

3066 Liposomal daunorubicin-cytarabine (CPX-351).[<a href="#cit/section_4.10">

306710</a>

3068] </li>

3069<li>

3070Intrathecal cytarabine or methotrexate may be used to treat central nervous system (CNS) leukemia, if present.</li>

3071</ul>

3072</div>

3073<p id="_55" tabindex="-1">

3074The two-drug regimen of cytarabine given as a continuous infusion for seven days and a three-day course of anthracycline (the so-called 7 + 3 induction therapy) results in a complete response rate of approximately 65%. In most instances, there is no further clinical benefit when adding potentially non-cross&#8722;resistant drugs (such as fludarabine, topoisomerase inhibitors, thioguanine, mitoxantrone, histone deacetylases inhibitors, or clofarabine) to a 7 + 3 regimen. Cladribine, when added to 7 + 3 induction chemotherapy, showed improved remission rates [<a href="#cit/section_4.11">

307511</a>

3076] and survival rates [<a href="#cit/section_4.12">

307712</a>

3078] across two randomized controlled trials, but this regimen has not been widely adopted in the absence of confirmatory trials. The addition of midostaurin and gemtuzumab ozogamicin to intensive induction chemotherapy is discussed below.</p>

3079<p id="_504" tabindex="-1">

3080The choice of anthracycline and the dose-intensity of anthracycline may influence the survival of patients with AML. Idarubicin appeared to be more effective than

3081daunorubicin, particularly in younger adults, although the doses of idarubicin and daunorubicin may not have

3082been equivalent.[<a href="#cit/section_4.3">

30833</a>

3084-<a href="#cit/section_4.6">

30856</a>

3086] No significant survival difference between daunorubicin and

3087mitoxantrone has been reported.[<a href="#cit/section_4.13">

308813</a>

3089]</p>

3090<section id="_651">

3091<h5 id="_651_toc">

3092Selection of an anthracycline</h5>

3093<p id="_631" tabindex="-1">

3094 At present, there is no conclusive evidence to recommend one anthracycline over another. </p>

3095<p id="_645" tabindex="-1">

3096Evidence (anthracycline):</p>

3097<div class="pdq-content-list">

3098<ol id="_609">

3099<li>

3100In a systematic review and meta-analysis, 18 randomized controlled trials that included 6,755 patients assessed the use of idarubicin versus daunorubicin as part of induction chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_4.14">

310114</a>

3102] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3103<ul id="_610">

3104<li>

3105The use of idarubicin lead to improved outcomes, including overall survival (OS) when compared with daunorubicin (12 studies, 5,976 patients; hazard ratio [HR], 0.90; 95% confidence interval [CI], 0.84&#8722;0.96; <em>

3106P</em>

3107 = .0008). However, there was an increased risk of death during induction (14 studies, 6,349 patients; relative risk [RR], 1.18; 95% CI, 1.01&#8722;1.36; <em>

3108P</em>

3109 = .03) and mucositis (five studies, 2,000 patients; RR, 1.22; 95% CI, 1.04&#8722;1.44; <em>

3110P</em>

3111 = .02) with idarubicin as compared with daunorubicin. Moreover, the survival benefit for idarubicin was no longer present if a daunorubicin dose of at least 180 mg/m<span class="sup">

31122</span>

3113 was used (four studies, 2,867 patients; HR, 0.91; 95% CI, 0.82&#8722;1.00; <em>

3114P</em>

3115 = .06).</li>

3116<li>

3117In patients aged 60 years and younger, outcomes for those who received daunorubicin (90 mg/m<span class="sup">

31182</span>

3119/dose, total induction dosing at 270 mg/m<span class="sup">

31202</span>

3121) were superior to those who received more traditional dosing (45 mg/m<span class="sup">

31222</span>

3123/dose; total dose = 135 mg/m<span class="sup">

31242</span>

3125). The complete remission (CR) rate was 71% versus 57% (<em>

3126P</em>

3127 &lt; .001), and the median survival was 24 months versus 16 months (<em>

3128P</em>

3129 = .003).[<a href="#cit/section_4.15">

313015</a>

3131]</li>

3132<li>

3133No randomized comparison data between daunorubicin at 270 mg/m<span class="sup">

31342</span>

3135 and daunorubicin at 180 mg/m<span class="sup">

31362</span>

3137, nor between daunorubicin at 270 mg/m<span class="sup">

31382</span>

3139 and idarubicin, are available. </li>

3140</ul>

3141</div>

3142</li>

3143</ol>

3144</div>

3145</section>

3146<section id="_652">

3147<h5 id="_652_toc">

3148Addition of midostaurin</h5>

3149<p id="_632" tabindex="-1">

3150Both mutations in the kinase domain and internal transmembrane duplications of the <em class="gene-name">

3151FLT3</em>

3152 gene are frequent in AML and are often associated with an inferior outcome.</p>

3153<p id="_646" tabindex="-1">

3154Evidence (midostaurin):</p>

3155<div class="pdq-content-list">

3156<ol id="_633">

3157<li>

3158In a multicenter, randomized phase III trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00651261">

3159NCT00651261</a>

3160), the addition of the FLT3/multikinase inhibitor midostaurin, versus placebo, to cytarabine and daunorubicin induction chemotherapy in patients with <em class="gene-name">

3161FLT3</em>

3162-mutated AML led to improved survival (median, 75 vs. 26 months; HR for death, 0.78; one-sided <em>

3163P</em>

3164 = .009).[<a href="#cit/section_4.8">

31658</a>

3166] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3167<ul id="_634">

3168<li>

3169OS and event-free survival (EFS) were better for patients on the midostaurin arm (HR for event or death, 0.78; one-sided <em>

3170P</em>

3171 = .002) and the survival benefit was consistent across all <em class="gene-name">

3172FLT3</em>

3173 mutation subtypes. The rates of CR (59% vs. 54%) and time to neutrophil count recovery were similar between the two arms.[<a href="#cit/section_4.8">

31748</a>

3175][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3176Level of evidence A1</a>

3177] </li>

3178</ul>

3179</div>

3180</li>

3181</ol>

3182</div>

3183</section>

3184<section id="_653">

3185<h5 id="_653_toc">

3186Addition of gemtuzumab ozogamicin</h5>

3187<p id="_635" tabindex="-1">

3188</p>

3189<p id="_647" tabindex="-1">

3190Evidence (gemtuzumab ozogamicin):</p>

3191<div class="pdq-content-list">

3192<ol id="_636">

3193<li>

3194In a meta-analysis of more than 3,000 patients, the addition of the CD33-directed immunotoxin gemtuzumab ozogamicin to cytarabine plus anthracycline or clofarabine plus anthracycline led to a small increase in the OS rate at 5 years (30.7% vs. 34.6%; HR, 0.90; 95% CI, 0.82&#8722;0.98; <em>

3195P</em>

3196 = .01).[<a href="#cit/section_4.9">

31979</a>

3198] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3199<ul id="_637">

3200<li>

3201The improvement in the 5-year OS rate was seen across all ages, but this effect was greatest in patients with favorable-risk cytogenetics (55.2% vs. 76.3%; HR, 0.47 [range, 0.31&#8722;0.73]; <em>

3202P</em>

3203 = .0005), and to a lesser extent with intermediate-risk cytogenetics (34.1% vs. 39.4%; HR, 0.84 [range, 0.75&#8722;0.95]; <em>

3204P</em>

3205 = .007). It was not seen in patients with an adverse-risk karyotype.[<a href="#cit/section_4.9">

32069</a>

3207][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3208Level of evidence A1</a>

3209] </li>

3210<li>

3211In contrast, gemtuzumab ozogamicin did not improve the 1-year survival rate of older patients who received low-dose cytarabine, although the CR rate increased from 17% to 30% (odds ratio [OR], 0.48 [range, 0.32&#8211;0.73]; <em>

3212P</em>

3213 = .006).[<a href="#cit/section_4.16">

321416</a>

3215] </li>

3216</ul>

3217</div>

3218<p id="_638" tabindex="-1">

3219The U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) label for gemtuzumab ozogamicin includes a boxed warning about the risk of hepatotoxicity, including severe or fatal hepatic sinusoidal obstruction syndrome.</p>

3220</li>

3221</ol>

3222</div>

3223</section>

3224<section id="_654">

3225<h5 id="_654_toc">

3226Liposomal daunorubicin-cytarabine (CPX-351)</h5>

3227<p id="_648" tabindex="-1">

3228CPX-351 is a two-drug liposomal encapsulation that delivers cytarabine and daunorubicin at a fixed 5:1 synergistic molar ratio.</p>

3229<p id="_649" tabindex="-1">

3230Evidence (CPX-351):</p>

3231<div class="pdq-content-list">

3232<ol id="_640">

3233<li>

3234A multicenter trial investigated CPX-351 in patients aged 60 to 75 years with therapy-related AML, AML with a history of myelodysplastic syndrome (MDS), or AML with myelodysplasia-related changes.[<a href="#cit/section_4.10">

323510</a>

3236] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3237<ul id="_641">

3238<li>

3239Compared with 7 + 3 induction chemotherapy, CPX-351 resulted in a better overall remission rate (47.7% vs. 33.3%; <em>

3240P</em>

3241 = .016), and improved median OS (9.56 vs. 5.95 months; HR, 0.69; 95% CI, 0.52&#8722;0.90; <em>

3242P</em>

3243 = .003).[<a href="#cit/section_4.10">

324410</a>

3245][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3246Level of evidence A1</a>

3247] </li>

3248<li>

3249The rates of early mortality and toxicities were similar between the two arms. However, the median time to recovery of neutrophils and platelets was longer for CPX-351 (35.0 and 36.5 days, respectively) as compared with 7 + 3 induction chemotherapy (29 and 29 days, respectively).</li>

3250</ul>

3251</div>

3252</li>

3253</ol>

3254</div>

3255</section>

3256<section id="_655">

3257<h5 id="_655_toc">

3258Older adults or adults with significant comorbid conditions</h5>

3259<p id="_613" tabindex="-1">

3260Some patients may decline or be too frail for intensive induction chemotherapy. Low-dose cytarabine, decitabine, azacitidine, or best supportive care can be considered equivalently effective treatment approaches for older patients with AML who decline traditional 7 + 3 induction chemotherapy. Unlike a succinct course of 7 + 3 induction, these less-intensive therapies are continued indefinitely, as long as the patient is deriving benefit (i.e., until disease progression or significant toxicity occurs). </p>

3261<p id="_614" tabindex="-1">

3262One of the following chemotherapy regimens may be used as less-intensive therapy:</p>

3263<div class="pdq-content-list">

3264<ul id="_615">

3265<li>

3266 Hypomethylating agents (azacitidine and decitabine).</li>

3267<li>

3268 Low-dose cytarabine.</li>

3269<li>

3270 Venetoclax plus hypomethylating agents or low-dose cytarabine.</li>

3271<li>

3272 Glasdegib plus low-dose cytarabine.</li>

3273<li>

3274 Ivosidenib with or without azacitidine.</li>

3275<li>

3276 Enasidenib.</li>

3277<li>

3278 Intrathecal cytarabine or methotrexate may be used to treat CNS leukemia, if present.</li>

3279</ul>

3280</div>

3281<p id="_511" tabindex="-1">

3282Evidence (chemotherapy for patients who decline intensive remission induction therapy):</p>

3283<div class="pdq-content-list">

3284<ol id="_512">

3285<li>

3286<strong>

3287Hypomethylating agents: </strong>

3288The hypomethylating agents azacitidine and decitabine are used commonly in this population of older patients, particularly in the United States. Although approval of the drugs by the FDA is for an MDS indication, the registration studies leading to approval included patients with 20% to 30% myeloblasts, or what would now be considered oligoblastic AML.[<a href="#cit/section_4.17">

328917</a>

3290,<a href="#cit/section_4.18">

329118</a>

3292]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3293<ol id="_616" class="lower-alpha">

3294<li>

3295<strong>

3296 Azacitidine:</strong>

3297 An international phase III trial (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01074047">

3298NCT01074047</a>

3299) randomly assigned patients with AML who were 65 years or older to receive either azacitidine or conventional regimens (7 + 3 induction, low-dose cytarabine, or best supportive care alone).[<a href="#cit/section_4.19">

330019</a>

3301] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3302<ul id="_620">

3303<li>

3304Azacitidine led to a median OS of 10.4 months (95% CI, 8.0&#8722;12.7) as compared with 6.5 months (95% CI, 5.0&#8722;8.6) with conventional regimens (HR, 0.85; 95% CI, 0.69&#8722;1.03; <em>

3305P</em>

3306 = .1009).[<a href="#cit/section_4.19">

330719</a>

3308][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3309Level of evidence A1</a>

3310]</li>

3311</ul>

3312</div>

3313</li>

3314<li>

3315<strong>

3316Decitabine: </strong>

3317One phase III trial randomly assigned 485 patients with AML who were older than 65 years to receive either decitabine (n = 242) or their preferred choice (n = 243) of either supportive care (n = 28) or low-dose cytarabine (n = 215).[<a href="#cit/section_4.20">

331820</a>

3319]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3320<ul id="_617">

3321<li>

3322Although rates of CR + CRp (CR with incomplete platelet recovery) were more than double in the decitabine arm (17.8%) compared with the treatment-choice arm (7.8%) (<em>

3323P</em>

3324 = .001), median OS was not significantly improved for patients receiving decitabine (7.7 months) compared with the treatment of choice (5.0 months) (HR for death for decitabine, 0.85; 95% CI, .69&#8211;1.04; <em>

3325P</em>

3326 = .11).</li>

3327</ul>

3328</div>

3329<p id="_618" tabindex="-1">

3330Compared with treatment for 5 consecutive days, treatment for 10 consecutive days may lead to higher response rates, particularly in those with <em class="gene-name">

3331TP53</em>

3332 mutations and/or unfavorable cytogenetic features.[<a href="#cit/section_4.21">

333321</a>

3334][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3335Level of evidence C3</a>

3336]</p>

3337</li>

3338</ol>

3339</div>

3340</li>

3341<li>

3342<strong>

3343Low-dose cytarabine: </strong>

3344 Older adults who decline intensive remission-induction therapy or are considered ineligible for intensive remission-induction therapy may derive benefit from low-dose cytarabine, administered twice daily for 10 days in cycles repeated every 4 to 6 weeks.[<a href="#cit/section_4.22">

334522</a>

3346] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3347<ul id="_513">

3348<li>

3349 The CR rate using this regimen was 18% compared with 1% for patients treated with hydroxyurea (<em>

3350P</em>

3351 = .006).</li>

3352<li>

3353Survival with low-dose cytarabine was better than was survival with hydroxyurea (OR, 0.60; 95% CI, 0.44&#8211;0.81; <em>

3354P</em>

3355 = .009).[<a href="#cit/section_4.22">

335622</a>

3357][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3358Level of evidence A1</a>

3359] </li>

3360</ul>

3361</div>

3362</li>

3363<li>

3364 <strong>

3365Venetoclax plus hypomethylating agents or low-dose cytarabine:</strong>

3366 The FDA approved venetoclax, an inhibitor of the anti-apoptotic protein BCL2, in combination with low-dose cytarabine or a hypomethylating agent for the treatment of AML in patients aged 75 years or older, and those who cannot undergo 7 + 3 induction chemotherapy because of comorbidities. Approval was granted based on the results of two studies.<div class="pdq-content-list">

3367<ol id="_621" class="lower-alpha">

3368<li>

3369The first study (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02203773">

3370NCT02203773</a>

3371) was a nonrandomized, open-label, phase Ib clinical trial of venetoclax in combination with azacitidine or decitabine.[<a href="#cit/section_4.23">

337223</a>

3373] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3374<ul id="_622">

3375<li>

3376In this study, 35 (61%; 95% CI, 47.6%&#8722;74.0%) of 57 patients had CR or CR with incomplete hematologic recovery (CRi). The median duration of response for all patients with a response (CR + CRi + partial remission [PR]) was 8.4 months (range, 4.7&#8722;11.7; n = 36).</li>

3377</ul>

3378</div>

3379</li>

3380<li>

3381 The second study (<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT02287233">

3382NCT02287233</a>

3383) was a phase I/IIb study of venetoclax in combination with low-dose cytarabine in 82 patients with newly diagnosed AML, including patients with previous exposure to a hypomethylating agent for an antecedent hematologic disorder such as MDS.[<a href="#cit/section_4.24">

338424</a>

3385] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3386<ul id="_623">

3387<li>

3388In the 82 patients enrolled in the study, the CR/CRi rate was 54% (95% CI, 42%&#8722;65%), with a median duration of remission of 8.1 months (95% CI, 5.3&#8722;14.9 months). The median OS for all patients, irrespective of response, was 10.1 months (95% CI, 5.7&#8722;14.2 months). </li>

3389<li>

3390The most common adverse events with venetoclax combinations are gastrointestinal symptoms and myelosuppression, which may require delays between cycles, growth factor support, or decreased duration of venetoclax administration per cycle. Additionally, appropriate prophylactic measures are typically taken to prevent tumor lysis syndrome.[<a href="#cit/section_4.24">

339124</a>

3392][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3393Level of evidence C3</a>

3394]</li>

3395</ul>

3396</div>

3397</li>

3398</ol>

3399</div>

3400</li>

3401<li>

3402 <strong>

3403Glasdegib plus low-dose cytarabine:</strong>

3404 Glasdegib, an oral inhibitor of the hedgehog pathway, combined with low-dose cytarabine was compared with low-dose cytarabine alone in a randomized, phase II open-label study that included 116 patients with AML who were aged 75 years or older or who had severe comorbid conditions (cardiac disease, renal impairment, or Eastern Cooperative Oncology Group performance status 2).[<a href="#cit/section_4.25">

340525</a>

3406] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3407<ul id="_624">

3408<li>

3409Of the 78 patients with AML who received glasdegib plus low-dose cytarabine, 24% (n = 19) of patients had a CR or CRi compared with 5% (2 of 38) of patients who received low-dose cytarabine alone. The median OS was 8.3 months (80%; CI, 6.6&#8211;9.5) for patients who received glasdegib/low-dose cytarabine and 4.3 months (80%; CI, 2.9&#8211;4.9) for patients who received low-dose cytarabine alone in patients with AML (HR, 0.46; 80% CI, 0.35&#8211;0.62; <em>

3410P</em>

3411&#8201;=&#8201;.0002).[<a href="#cit/section_4.25">

341225</a>

3413][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3414Level of evidence A1</a>

3415]</li>

3416</ul>

3417</div>

3418<p id="_625" tabindex="-1">

3419Similar to venetoclax, the FDA approved glasdegib in combination with low-dose cytarabine for the treatment of AML in patients aged 75 years or older or who are unable to receive intensive induction chemotherapy.</p>

3420</li>

3421<li>

3422<strong>

3423 Ivosidenib:</strong>

3424 For older or frail patients with AML that harbors an <em class="gene-name">

3425IDH1</em>

3426 mutation, the IDH1 inhibitor ivosidenib is an option. The FDA approved ivosidenib alone or in combination with azacitidine for the treatment of AML that has a susceptible <em class="gene-name">

3427IDH1</em>

3428 mutation (detected by an FDA-approved diagnostic test) in adults aged 75 years or older with newly diagnosed AML or who have comorbidities that preclude the use of intensive induction chemotherapy. Within the context of a phase I study, 34 patients with newly diagnosed <em class="gene-name">

3429IDH1</em>

3430-mutated AML who were not candidates for intensive induction chemotherapy were treated with single-agent ivosidenib.[<a href="#cit/section_4.26">

343126</a>

3432]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3433<ul id="_626">

3434<li>

3435Differentiation syndrome was reported in 6 patients (18%), but did not require treatment discontinuation. </li>

3436<li>

3437The rate of CR plus CRi was 42.4% (95% CI, 25.5%&#8722;60.8%), with a median duration of response that was not reached (lower bound of the 95% CI was 4.6 months). </li>

3438<li>

3439For all 34 patients on the study, the median OS was 12.6 months (95% CI, 4.5&#8722;25.7).[<a href="#cit/section_4.26">

344026</a>

3441][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3442Level of evidence C3</a>

3443]</li>

3444</ul>

3445</div>

3446<p id="_794" tabindex="-1">

3447The combination of azacitidine and ivosidenib was evaluated in a double-blind, randomized, placebo-controlled, phase III trial in patients with newly diagnosed AML who were not eligible for intensive induction chemotherapy. The intention-to-treat analysis included 72 patients treated with azacitidine and ivosidenib and 74 patients treated with azacitidine and placebo. A supplemental new drug application for ivosidenib in combination with azacitidine for patients with untreated <em class="gene-name">

3448IDH1</em>

3449-mutated AML is under priority review with the FDA.[<a href="#cit/section_4.27">

345027</a>

3451]</p>

3452<div class="pdq-content-list">

3453<ul id="_795">

3454<li>

3455At a median follow-up of 12.4 months, the primary end point of EFS was improved in patients who received azacitidine and ivosidenib, compared with patients who received azacitidine and placebo (HR, 0.33; 95% CI, 0.16&#8211;0.69).</li>

3456<li>

3457 The median OS was 24 months for patients who received azacitidine and ivosidenib and 7.9 months for patients who received azacitidine and placebo (HR for death, 0.44; 95% CI, 0.27&#8211;0.73).</li>

3458<li>

3459 Differentiation syndrome occurred in 14% of patients who received azacitidine and ivosidenib and 8% of patients who received azacitidine and placebo. The incidence of bleeding events was 41% with azacitidine and ivosidenib and 29% with azacitidine and placebo. Infection of any grade was seen in 28% of patients who received azacitidine and ivosidenib and 49% of patients who received azacitidine and placebo. For more information about differentiation syndrome, see the <a href="/types/leukemia/hp/adult-aml-treatment-pdq#_690">

3460Treatment of Newly Diagnosed Acute Promeylocytic Leukemia</a>

3461 section.[<a href="#cit/section_4.27">

346227</a>

3463][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3464Level of evidence A1</a>

3465] </li>

3466</ul>

3467</div>

3468</li>

3469<li>

3470 <strong>

3471Enasidenib:</strong>

3472 For patients with an AML that harbors a mutation in <em class="gene-name">

3473IDH2</em>

3474, the IDH2 inhibitor enasidenib is an option for older or frail patients. Although it does not have approval in this setting, enasidenib monotherapy was evaluated in a phase I/II trial in patients with newly diagnosed AML who were not eligible for standard chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_4.28">

347528</a>

3476] <div class="pdq-content-list">

3477<ul id="_627">

3478<li>

3479Of the 39 patients enrolled, seven (18%) had CR, one (3%) had CRi, and two (5%) had a PR. </li>

3480<li>

3481Median OS for all patients was 11.3 months (95% CI, 5.7&#8722;15.1), and was not reached for patients who had a response.[<a href="#cit/section_4.28">

348228</a>

3483][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3484Level of evidence C3</a>

3485]</li>

3486</ul>

3487</div>

3488</li>

3489</ol>

3490</div>

3500 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

3626 <section id="_67">

3627

3628 <h2>

3629Treatment of AML in Remission</h2>

3630

3631 <div id="_section_67" class="pdq-sections">

3632<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

3633<h6>

3634In This Section</h6>

3635<ul>

3636<li>

3637<a href="#_529_toc">

3638Chemotherapy</a>

3639</li>

3640<li>

3641<a href="#_705_toc">

3642Maintenance Therapy<ul>

3643<li>

3644<a href="#_662_toc">

3645Midostaurin</a>

3646</li>

3647<li>

3648<a href="#_668_toc">

3649Oral azacitidine</a>

3650</li>

3651</ul>

3652</a>

3653</li>

3654<li>

3655<a href="#_532_toc">

3656Hematopoietic Cell (Bone Marrow or Stem Cell) Transplantation<ul>

3657<li>

3658<a href="#_533_toc">

3659Allogeneic HCT</a>

3660</li>

3661<li>

3662<a href="#_538_toc">

3663Autologous hematopoietic stem cell transplantation</a>

3664</li>

3665</ul>

3666</a>

3667</li>

3668<li>

3669<a href="#_TrialSearch_67_sid_5_toc">

3670Current Clinical Trials</a>

3671</li>

3672</ul>

3673</nav>

3674<p id="_69" tabindex="-1">

3675Although individual patients with acute myeloid leukemia (AML) have been reported to have long disease-free

3676survival (DFS) or cure with a single cycle of chemotherapy,[<a href="#cit/section_5.1">

36771</a>

3678] postremission therapy

3679is always indicated in therapy that is planned with curative intent. In a

3680small randomized study conducted by the Eastern Cooperative Oncology Group, all

3681patients who did not receive postremission therapy experienced a relapse after

3682a short median complete remission (CR) duration.[<a href="#cit/section_5.2">

36832</a>

3684]

3685</p>

3686<p id="_526" tabindex="-1">

3687Treatment options for AML in remission (postremission phase) include the following:</p>

3688<div class="pdq-content-list">

3689<ol id="_527">

3690<li>

3691<a href="/types/leukemia/hp/adult-aml-treatment-pdq#_529">

3692Chemotherapy</a>

3693 with short-term (3&#8722;4 cycles), relatively intensive chemotherapy

3694with cytarabine-based regimens similar to standard induction clinical trials

3695(postremission chemotherapy) and postremission chemotherapy with more

3696dose-intensive cytarabine-based treatment.</li>

3697<li>

3698<a href="/types/leukemia/hp/adult-aml-treatment-pdq#_705">

3699 Maintenance therapy</a>

3700 (longer-term therapy at lower doses) has not been shown to benefit AML patients in a number of studies, but two strategies have shown a benefit:<div class="pdq-content-list">

3701<ul id="_659">

3702<li>

3703 <a href="/types/leukemia/hp/adult-aml-treatment-pdq#_662">

3704Midostaurin</a>

3705 in patients with <em class="gene-name">

3706FLT3</em>

3707-mutated AML. </li>

3708<li>

3709 <a href="/types/leukemia/hp/adult-aml-treatment-pdq#_668">

3710Oral azacitidine</a>

3711.

3712</li>

3713</ul>

3714</div>

3715</li>

3716<li>

3717<a href="/types/leukemia/hp/adult-aml-treatment-pdq#_532">

3718Hematopoietic cell (bone marrow or stem cell) transplantation</a>

3719.<div class="pdq-content-list">

3720<ul id="_575">

3721<li>

3722High-dose chemotherapy with autologous peripheral blood stem cell rescue.</li>

3723<li>

3724High-dose

3725marrow-ablative or reduced-intensity therapy followed by allogeneic hematopoietic cell transplantation (HCT).</li>

3726</ul>

3727</div>

3728</li>

3729</ol>

3730</div>

3731<section id="_529">

3732<h3 id="_529_toc">

3733Chemotherapy</h3>

3734<p id="_70" tabindex="-1">

3735Nontransplant postremission therapy using cytarabine-containing regimens has

3736treatment-related death rates that are usually less than 10% to 20% and has

3737reported long-term DFS rates from 20% to 50%.[<a href="#cit/section_5.3">

37383</a>

3739-<a href="#cit/section_5.6">

37406</a>

3741] The optimal doses,

3742schedules, and duration of postremission chemotherapy have not been determined.</p>

3743<p id="_576" tabindex="-1">

3744The standard postremission therapy for AML patients in remission is high-dose cytarabine; however, there exists some controversy about whether it benefits all younger AML patients in first complete response versus selected subgroups, such as those with core-binding factor abnormalities.[<a href="#cit/section_5.7">

37457</a>

3746-<a href="#cit/section_5.11">

374711</a>

3748] The duration of postremission therapy has

3749ranged from one cycle [<a href="#cit/section_5.4">

37504</a>

3751,<a href="#cit/section_5.6">

37526</a>

3753] to four or more cycles.[<a href="#cit/section_5.3">

37543</a>

3755,<a href="#cit/section_5.5">

37565</a>

3757]</p>

3758<p id="_530" tabindex="-1">

3759Evidence (chemotherapy):</p>

3760<div class="pdq-content-list">

3761<ol id="_531">

3762<li>

3763A large,

3764randomized trial that compared three different cytarabine-containing

3765postremission therapy regimens showed a clear benefit in survival to patients younger

3766than 60 years who received high-dose cytarabine.[<a href="#cit/section_5.3">

37673</a>

3768]</li>

3769<li>

3770Intensification of

3771cytarabine dose or duration of postremission chemotherapy with conventionally dosed cytarabine did not improve DFS or overall survival (OS) in patients aged 60 years or older, as evidenced in the Medical Research Council (MRC-LEUK-AML11) trial.[<a href="#cit/section_5.12">

377212</a>

3773,<a href="#cit/section_5.13">

377413</a>

3775]</li>

3776</ol>

3777</div>

3778<p id="_71" tabindex="-1">

3779Dose-intensive cytarabine-based chemotherapy can be complicated by severe

3780neurologic [<a href="#cit/section_5.14">

378114</a>

3782] and/or pulmonary toxic effects [<a href="#cit/section_5.15">

378315</a>

3784] and should be administered

3785by physicians experienced in these regimens at centers that are equipped to

3786treat potential complications. In a retrospective analysis of 256 patients

3787who received high-dose bolus cytarabine at a single institution, the most

3788powerful predictor of cytarabine neurotoxicity was renal insufficiency. The

3789incidence of neurotoxicity was significantly greater in patients treated with

3790twice daily doses of 3 g/m<span class="sup">

37912</span>

3792/dose when compared with 2

3793g/m<span class="sup">

37942</span>

3795/dose.</p>

3796</section>

3797<section id="_705">

3798<h3 id="_705_toc">

3799Maintenance Therapy</h3>

3800<p id="_661" tabindex="-1">

3801While a number of older studies have included longer-term therapy at lower doses (maintenance), there has been no convincing evidence that maintenance therapy provides prolonged DFS or OS. However, maintenance therapy with midostaurin or oral azacitidine may improve outcomes.</p>

3802<section id="_662">

3803<h4 id="_662_toc">

3804Midostaurin</h4>

3805<p id="_663" tabindex="-1">

3806Evidence (midostaurin):</p>

3807<p id="_664" tabindex="-1">

3808Mutations in the kinase domain and internal transmembrane duplications of the <em class="gene-name">

3809FLT3</em>

3810 gene are frequent in AML and are often associated with an inferior outcome.</p>

3811<div class="pdq-content-list">

3812<ol id="_665">

3813<li>

3814In the multicenter, randomized phase III <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00651261">

3815RATIFY</a>

3816 trial (NCT00651261), the FLT3/multikinase inhibitor midostaurin plus cytarabine and daunorubicin induction chemotherapy was compared with placebo in patients with <em class="gene-name">

3817FLT3</em>

3818-mutated AML.[<a href="#cit/section_5.16">

381916</a>

3820][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3821Level of evidence A1</a>

3822]<div class="pdq-content-list">

3823<ul id="_666">

3824<li>

3825 The addition of the FLT3/multikinase inhibitor midostaurin to cytarabine and daunorubicin induction chemotherapy led to improved survival (median, 75 vs. 26 months; hazard ratio [HR] for death, 0.78; one-sided <em>

3826P</em>

3827 = .009).</li>

3828<li>

3829Patients who remained in remission after completion of consolidation therapy entered a maintenance phase in which they received midostaurin or placebo, administered at a dose of 50 mg orally twice daily, for twelve 28-day cycles. A maintenance regimen was administered for the full 12 cycles in 120 patients (69 in the midostaurin group, and 51 in the placebo group). </li>

3830<li>

3831An ad-hoc landmark analysis from the end of maintenance revealed no difference in DFS between the two arms. Moreover, from the start of maintenance therapy there was no difference in OS between the two arms.[<a href="#cit/section_5.17">

383217</a>

3833] </li>

3834</ul>

3835</div>

3836<p id="_667" tabindex="-1">

3837While maintenance was well tolerated in the RATIFY study, only a small subset of patients tolerated midostaurin as maintenance therapy after chemotherapy or transplantation in a separate phase II study.[<a href="#cit/section_5.18">

383818</a>

3839]</p>

3840</li>

3841<li>

3842 In the multicenter, randomized phase II <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01883362">

3843RADIUS</a>

3844 trial (NCT01883362), the addition of midostaurin to standard of care was compared with standard of care alone after allogeneic HCT.[<a href="#cit/section_5.19">

384519</a>

3846] Similar to the RATIFY trial, midostaurin was administered at a dose of 50 mg orally twice daily, for twelve 28-day cycles. Thirty patients were enrolled in each arm, but only half were able to complete the entire 12 cycles of therapy. <div class="pdq-content-list">

3847<ul id="_672">

3848<li>

3849The estimated 18-month relapse-free survival (RFS) rate was 89% in the midostaurin arm and 76% in the standard of care arm (HR, 0.46; 95% confidence interval [CI], 0.12&#8722;1.86; <em>

3850P</em>

3851 = 0.27). The predicted relative reduction in the risk of relapse with the addition of midostaurin was 54%.[<a href="#cit/section_5.19">

385219</a>

3853][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810025&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3854Level of evidence B1</a>

3855]</li>

3856</ul>

3857</div>

3858</li>

3859</ol>

3860</div>

3861</section>

3862<section id="_668">

3863<h4 id="_668_toc">

3864Oral azacitidine</h4>

3865<p id="_669" tabindex="-1">

3866Evidence (oral azacitidine): </p>

3867<div class="pdq-content-list">

3868<ol id="_670">

3869<li>

3870The randomized, double-blind, placebo-controlled phase III <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT01757535">

3871QUAZAR AML-001</a>

3872 trial (NCT01757535) provided the basis for regulatory approval of oral azacitidine as maintenance therapy for AML.[<a href="#cit/section_5.20">

387320</a>

3874] The study included 472 patients with AML who were aged 55 years or older, were within 4 months of first CR or CR with incomplete hematologic recovery after induction chemotherapy with or without consolidation treatment, and were not candidates for allogeneic HCT. Oral azacitidine or placebo was administered at 300 mg daily for 14 days every 28 days. Treatment was continued until disease progression or unacceptable toxicity. <div class="pdq-content-list">

3875<ul id="_671">

3876<li>

3877For patients who received azacitidine, the median OS from randomization was 24.7 months (95% CI, 18.7&#8722;30.5) compared with 14.8 months (95% CI, 11.7&#8722;17.6) for patients receiving placebo (HR, 0.69; 95% CI, 0.55&#8722;0.86; <em>

3878P</em>

3879 = .0009).[<a href="#cit/section_5.20">

388020</a>

3881][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3882Level of evidence A1</a>

3883]</li>

3884</ul>

3885</div>

3886</li>

3887</ol>

3888</div>

3889</section>

3890</section>

3891<section id="_532">

3892<h3 id="_532_toc">

3893Hematopoietic Cell (Bone Marrow or Stem Cell) Transplantation</h3>

3894<section id="_533">

3895<h4 id="_533_toc">

3896Allogeneic HCT</h4>

3897<p id="_72" tabindex="-1">

3898Allogeneic HCT, even with minimal conditioning chemotherapy, results in the lowest incidence of

3899leukemic relapse, even when compared with HCT from an

3900identical twin (syngeneic HCT). This finding led to the

3901concept of an immunologic graft-versus-leukemia effect, similar to (and related

3902to) graft-versus-host disease. The improvement in freedom from relapse using

3903allogeneic HCT as the primary postremission therapy is

3904offset, at least in part, by the increased morbidity and mortality caused by

3905graft-versus-host disease, veno-occlusive disease of the liver, and

3906infection. The DFS rates using allogeneic

3907transplantation in first complete remission have ranged from 45% to 60%.[<a href="#cit/section_5.21">

390821</a>

3909-<a href="#cit/section_5.24">

391024</a>

3911]

3912</p>

3913<p id="_534" tabindex="-1">

3914The use of allogeneic HCT in adults requires either a human leukocyte antigen (HLA)-matched

3915sibling donor, an HLA-matched unrelated donor, a haploidentical donor (&#8220;half HLA-matched&#8221;), or two well-matched umbilical cord blood units. Including patients who underwent HCT from 2007 to 2017, the 3-year probabilities of survival after HLA-matched sibling transplant were 59% (&#177;1%) for patients with early disease, 53% (&#177;1%) for patients with intermediate disease, and 29% (&#177;1%) for patients with advanced disease, according to the Center for International Blood and Marrow Transplant Research registry.[<a href="#cit/section_5.24">

391624</a>

3917] The probabilities of survival after an unrelated donor transplant were 53% (&#177;1%) for patients with early disease, 50% (&#177;1%) for intermediate disease, and 27% (&#177;1%) for patients with advanced disease. [<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3918Level of evidence C1</a>

3919]</p>

3920<p id="_78" tabindex="-1">

3921Because HCT can cure more than 30% of patients who

3922experience relapse after chemotherapy, some investigators suggested that

3923allogeneic bone marrow transplant (BMT) can be reserved for early first relapse

3924or second CR without compromising the number of patients who

3925are ultimately cured.[<a href="#cit/section_5.25">

392625</a>

3927] Clinical and cytogenetic information can

3928define certain subsets of patients with predictable better or worse prognoses

3929according to favorable- and adverse-risk factors in those using postremission chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_5.26">

393026</a>

3931] </p>

3932<div class="pdq-content-list">

3933<ul id="_543">

3934<li>

3935<strong>

3936Favorable-risk AML:</strong>

3937 Favorable-risk factors include t(8;21),

3938inv(16), normal karyotype with <em class="gene-name">

3939NPM1</em>

3940 mutation (in absence of <em class="gene-name">

3941FLT3</em>

3942 mutation), and normal karyotype with double cytosine-cytosine-adenosine-adenosine-thymidine (CCAAT)-enhancer binding protein (C/EBP)-alpha mutations. Patients in the favorable-risk group have a reasonable chance of cure with intensive

3943postremission chemotherapy, and it may be reasonable to defer transplantation in that group

3944until early first relapse. </li>

3945<li>

3946<strong>

3947Adverse-risk AML:</strong>

3948 Adverse-risk factors include deletion of 5q, 7q, 17p, inversion of 3 or t(3;3), abnormality of (17p), trisomy 8, t(6;9),

3949t(9;22), most translocations involving chromosome 11q23, and mutations of the <em class="gene-name">

3950MLL</em>

3951 gene, a complex or monosomal karyotype, a history of myelodysplasia or antecedent hematologic disorder, <em class="gene-name">

3952TP53</em>

3953 mutation, <em class="gene-name">

3954RUNX1</em>

3955 mutation, <em class="gene-name">

3956ASXL1</em>

3957 mutation, and normal karyotype with <em class="gene-name">

3958FLT3</em>

3959 mutation.

3960The adverse-risk group is highly unlikely to be cured with

3961postremission chemotherapy, and allogeneic BMT in first CR is a reasonable option for patients. However, even with allogeneic stem cell transplantation, the

3962outcome for patients with high-risk AML is poor (5-year DFS

3963rate of 8% to 30% for patients with treatment-related leukemia or

3964myelodysplasia).[<a href="#cit/section_5.27">

396527</a>

3966]</li>

3967<li>

3968<strong>

3969Normal cytogenetics:</strong>

3970 Patients with normal cytogenetics are in an intermediate-risk

3971group, and postremission management should be individualized based on additional molecular markers, patient comorbid factors, and patient preference or, preferably, managed according to a clinical trial.

3972</li>

3973</ul>

3974</div>

3975<p id="_342" tabindex="-1">

3976A common clinical trial design used to evaluate the benefit of allogeneic transplant as consolidation therapy for AML in first remission is the so-called <em>

3977donor-no donor</em>

3978 comparison. In this design, newly diagnosed AML patients who achieve a CR are deemed medically eligible for allogeneic transplant and undergo HLA typing. If a matched sibling or matched unrelated donor is identified, the patient is allocated to the transplantation arm. Analysis of outcome is by intention to treat; that is, patients assigned to the donor arm who do not receive a transplant are grouped in the analysis with the patients who did actually receive a transplant. RFS is the usual end point for this type of trial. OS from the time of diagnosis is less frequently reported in these trials. </p>

3979<p id="_341" tabindex="-1">

3980 Investigators attempted to address this issue with a meta-analysis using data from 18 separate prospective trials of AML patients using the <em>

3981donor-no donor</em>

3982 design, with data from an additional six trials included for sensitivity analysis.[<a href="#cit/section_5.28">

398328</a>

3984] The trials included in this meta-analysis enrolled adult patients aged 60 years and younger from 1982 to 2006. Median follow-up ranged from 42 months to 142 months. Preparative regimens were similar among the different trials. Allogeneic transplant was compared with autologous transplant (six trials) or with a variety of consolidation chemotherapy regimens, with high-dose cytarabine being the most common.</p>

3985<div class="pdq-content-list">

3986<ul id="_535">

3987<li>

3988Treatment-related mortality ranged from 5% to 42% in the donor groups compared with 3% to 27% in the no-donor group.</li>

3989<li>

3990Of 18 trials reporting RFS across all cytogenetic risk groups, the combined HR for overall RFS benefit with allogeneic transplant was 0.80, indicating a statistically significant reduction in death or relapse in a first CR.</li>

3991<li>

3992Of the 15 trials reporting OS across all cytogenetic risk groups, the combined HR for OS was 0.90, again indicating a statistically significant reduction in death or relapse in a first CR.</li>

3993<li>

3994In subgroup analysis according to cytogenetic risk , there was no RFS or OS benefit of allogeneic transplant for patients with favorable-risk AML (RFS: HR, 1.07; 95% CI, 0.83&#8211;1.38; <em>

3995P</em>

3996 = .59; OS: HR, 1.06; 95% CI, 0.64&#8211;1.76; <em>

3997P</em>

3998 = .81). However, a transplant benefit was seen for patients with intermediate (RFS: HR, 0.83; 95% CI, 0.74&#8211;0.93; <em>

3999P</em>

4000 &lt; .01; OS: HR, 0.84; 95% CI, 0.71&#8211;0.99; <em>

4001P</em>

4002 = .03) or adverse-risk cytogenetics (RFS: HR, 0.73; 95% CI, 0.59&#8211;0.90; <em>

4003P</em>

4004 &lt; .01; OS: HR, 0.60; 95% CI, 0.40&#8211;0.90; <em>

4005P </em>

4006= .01).[<a href="#cit/section_5.28">

400728</a>

4008][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4009Level of evidence B4</a>

4010] The conclusion from this meta-analysis was that allogeneic transplant from a sibling donor in a first CR is justified on the basis of improved RFS and OS for patients with intermediate- or adverse-risk, but not favorable-risk, cytogenetics.<p id="_536" tabindex="-1">

4011An important caveat to this analysis is that induction and postremission strategies for AML among studies included in the meta-analysis were not uniform; nor were definitions of cytogenetic risk groups uniform. This may have resulted in inferior survival rates among chemotherapy-only treated patients. </p>

4012</li>

4013</ul>

4014</div>

4015<p id="_537" tabindex="-1">

4016Most physicians who treat patients with leukemia agree that transplantation should be offered to AML patients in first CR in the setting of adverse-risk cytogenetics and should not be offered to patients in first CR with favorable-risk cytogenetics.[<a href="#cit/section_5.26">

401726</a>

4018] However, older patients with favorable-risk AML who are unlikely to tolerate intensive cytarabine-based consolidation therapy can be considered for allogeneic HCT as postremission therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_5.29">

401929</a>

4020]</p>

4021</section>

4022<section id="_538">

4023<h4 id="_538_toc">

4024Autologous hematopoietic stem cell transplantation</h4>

4025<p id="_73" tabindex="-1">

4026The role of autologous transplantation for AML patients has diminished over time because of the improvements in the nonrelapse mortality associated with allogeneic HCT, as well as the advent of haploidentical and umbilical cord transplantation expanding the potential donor pool so that nearly every patient has a donor.[<a href="#cit/section_5.30">

402730</a>

4028-<a href="#cit/section_5.33">

402933</a>

4030] Autologous HCT can yield DFS rates

4031between 35% and 50% in patients with AML in first remission. Autologous HCT has also cured a smaller proportion of patients in second

4032remission.[<a href="#cit/section_5.34">

403334</a>

4034-<a href="#cit/section_5.40">

403540</a>

4036] Treatment-related mortality rates of patients who have had

4037autologous peripheral blood or marrow transplantation range from 10% to 20%.

4038</p>

4039</section>

4040</section>

4041<section id="_TrialSearch_67_sid_5">

4042<h3 id="_TrialSearch_67_sid_5_toc">

4043Current Clinical Trials</h3>

4044<p id="_TrialSearch_67_22" tabindex="-1">

4045Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

4046advanced clinical trial search</a>

4047 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

4048General information</a>

4049 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

4217 <section id="_80">

4218

4219 <h2>

4220Treatment of Refractory or Recurrent AML</h2>

4221

4222 <div id="_section_80" class="pdq-sections">

4223<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

4224<h6>

4225In This Section</h6>

4226<ul>

4227<li>

4228<a href="#_554_toc">

4229Chemotherapy<ul>

4230<li>

4231<a href="#_784_toc">

4232Intensive salvage chemotherapy</a>

4233</li>

4234<li>

4235<a href="#_785_toc">

4236Reduced-intensity therapy, including targeted therapy</a>

4237</li>

4238</ul>

4239</a>

4240</li>

4241<li>

4242<a href="#_560_toc">

4243Allogeneic Hematopoietic Cell Transplantation</a>

4244</li>

4245<li>

4246<a href="#_TrialSearch_80_sid_6_toc">

4247Current Clinical Trials</a>

4248</li>

4249</ul>

4250</nav>

4251<p id="_263" tabindex="-1">

4252No standard treatment regimen exists for patients with refractory or recurrent acute myeloid leukemia (AML).[<a href="#cit/section_6.1">

42531</a>

4254,<a href="#cit/section_6.2">

42552</a>

4256]</p>

4257<p id="_552" tabindex="-1">

4258Treatment options for refractory or recurrent AML include the following:</p>

4259<div class="pdq-content-list">

4260<ol id="_553">

4261<li>

4262<a href="/types/leukemia/hp/adult-aml-treatment-pdq#_554">

4263Chemotherapy</a>

4264.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4265<ul id="_702">

4266<li>

4267<a href="/types/leukemia/hp/adult-aml-treatment-pdq#_784">

4268Intensive salvage chemotherapy</a>

4269.</li>

4270<li>

4271<a href="/types/leukemia/hp/adult-aml-treatment-pdq#_785">

4272Reduced-intensity therapy, including targeted therapy</a>

4273.</li>

4274</ul>

4275</div>

4276</li>

4277<li>

4278<a href="/types/leukemia/hp/adult-aml-treatment-pdq#_560">

4279Allogeneic hematopoietic cell transplantation (HCT)</a>

4280.</li>

4281</ol>

4282</div>

4283<section id="_554">

4284<h3 id="_554_toc">

4285Chemotherapy</h3>

4286<section id="_784">

4287<h4 id="_784_toc">

4288Intensive salvage chemotherapy</h4>

4289<p id="_82" tabindex="-1">

4290A number of intensive salvage chemotherapy regimens have demonstrated efficacy in recurrent AML, including the following:</p>

4291<section id="_725">

4292<h5 id="_725_toc">

4293Fludarabine, cytarabine, and filgrastim (FLAG)</h5>

4294<p id="_737" tabindex="-1">

4295FLAG has shown antileukemic activity in patients with relapsed and refractory AML.</p>

4296<p id="_738" tabindex="-1">

4297Evidence (FLAG):</p>

4298<div class="pdq-content-list">

4299<ol id="_739">

4300<li>

4301A multicenter phase II study included 83 patients with relapsed or refractory AML or de novo refractory anemia with excess blasts in transformation. The primary end point was the rate of complete remission (CR) achieved after one or two courses of FLAG induction chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_6.3">

43023</a>

4303] <div class="pdq-content-list">

4304<ul id="_740">

4305<li>

4306In patients with relapsed leukemia whose first remission lasted for 6 months or more, the CR rate was 81% (17 out of 21 patients). </li>

4307<li>

4308In patients with AML whose first remission lasted less than 6 months, or in patients with primary refractory disease, the CR rate was 30% (13 out of 44 patients).[<a href="#cit/section_6.3">

43093</a>

4310][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4311Level of evidence C3</a>

4312]</li>

4313<li>

4314Myelosuppression and mucositis were common therapy-related toxicities.</li>

4315</ul>

4316</div>

4317</li>

4318</ol>

4319</div>

4320<p id="_741" tabindex="-1">

4321Idarubicin has been added to this regimen as well (FLAG-Ida).[<a href="#cit/section_6.4">

43224</a>

4323]</p>

4324</section>

4325<section id="_727">

4326<h5 id="_727_toc">

4327Mitoxantrone, etoposide, and cytarabine (MEC)</h5>

4328<p id="_742" tabindex="-1">

4329Evidence (MEC):</p>

4330<div class="pdq-content-list">

4331<ol id="_743">

4332<li>

4333A study evaluated one course of MEC chemotherapy in 74 patients with AML and a poor prognosis. The population included 30 patients with relapsed AML, 28 patients with primary refractory AML, and 16 patients with secondary AML.[<a href="#cit/section_6.5">

43345</a>

4335]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4336<ul id="_744">

4337<li>

4338 MEC demonstrated a CR induction rate of 55%.[<a href="#cit/section_6.5">

43395</a>

4340][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4341Level of evidence C3</a>

4342] </li>

4343</ul>

4344</div>

4345</li>

4346<li>

4347A phase III randomized Eastern Cooperative Oncology Group (ECOG) trial (E-2995) assessed 129 patients with one of the following disease statuses: relapsed AML less than 6 months after first CR; relapsed AML after allogeneic or autologous bone marrow transplantation; second or greater AML relapse; primary induction failure; secondary AML; or high-risk myelodysplastic syndromes. Patients were randomly assigned to receive MEC with or without valspodar, a multidrug resistance modulator.<div class="pdq-content-list">

4348<ul id="_745">

4349<li>

4350The complete response rate was only 17% to 25% in both arms.[<a href="#cit/section_6.6">

43516</a>

4352][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810031&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4353Level of evidence B3</a>

4354]</li>

4355</ul>

4356</div>

4357</li>

4358</ol>

4359</div>

4360</section>

4361<section id="_729">

4362<h5 id="_729_toc">

4363Standard or high-dose cytarabine and mitoxantrone</h5>

4364<p id="_748" tabindex="-1">

4365Evidence (standard or high-dose cytarabine and mitoxantrone):</p>

4366<div class="pdq-content-list">

4367<ol id="_749">

4368<li>

4369A study of cytarabine and mitoxantrone included 49 patients with relapsed or refractory AML.[<a href="#cit/section_6.7">

43707</a>

4371]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4372<ul id="_750">

4373<li>

4374Treatment was successful in 50% to 60% of patients who

4375experienced relapse after initially obtaining a CR, with 62.5% of patients with AML in first relapse achieving M1 marrow.[<a href="#cit/section_6.7">

43767</a>

4377,<a href="#cit/section_6.8">

43788</a>

4379] </li>

4380</ul>

4381</div>

4382</li>

4383</ol>

4384</div>

4385</section>

4386<section id="_731">

4387<h5 id="_731_toc">

4388High-dose etoposide and cyclophosphamide</h5>

4389<p id="_751" tabindex="-1">

4390Evidence (high-dose etoposide and cyclophosphamide):</p>

4391<div class="pdq-content-list">

4392<ol id="_752">

4393<li>

4394 Reported results have been similar to those for the combination of cytarabine and mitoxantrone.[<a href="#cit/section_6.9">

43959</a>

4396]</li>

4397</ol>

4398</div>

4399</section>

4400<section id="_733">

4401<h5 id="_733_toc">

4402Idarubicin and cytarabine</h5>

4403<p id="_753" tabindex="-1">

4404Evidence (idarubicin and cytarabine):</p>

4405<div class="pdq-content-list">

4406<ol id="_790">

4407<li>

4408 Reported results have been similar to those for the combination of cytarabine and mitoxantrone.[<a href="#cit/section_6.10">

440910</a>

4410,<a href="#cit/section_6.11">

441111</a>

4412]</li>

4413</ol>

4414</div>

4415</section>

4416<section id="_735">

4417<h5 id="_735_toc">

4418Other intensive regimens</h5>

4419<div class="pdq-content-list">

4420<ul id="_736">

4421<li>

4422High-dose cytarabine.[<a href="#cit/section_6.12">

442312</a>

4424] </li>

4425<li>

4426Cytarabine, daunorubicin, and etoposide (ADE).[<a href="#cit/section_6.13">

442713</a>

4428] </li>

4429<li>

4430Clofarabine plus cytarabine with or without filgrastim (CLAG).[<a href="#cit/section_6.14">

443114</a>

4432,<a href="#cit/section_6.15">

443315</a>

4434] </li>

4435</ul>

4436</div>

4437</section>

4438</section>

4439<section id="_785">

4440<h4 id="_785_toc">

4441Reduced-intensity therapy, including targeted therapy</h4>

4442<p id="_557" tabindex="-1">

4443Patients who are unable or unwilling to undergo intensive therapy can be treated with reduced-intensity therapies, including the following:</p>

4444<section id="_746">

4445<h5 id="_746_toc">

4446Gilteritinib</h5>

4447<p id="_747" tabindex="-1">

4448Gilteritinib is an oral FLT3 inhibitor with activity in both internal tandem duplication (ITD) and tyrosine kinase domain (TKD) subtypes. </p>

4449<p id="_754" tabindex="-1">

4450Evidence (gilteritinib):</p>

4451<div class="pdq-content-list">

4452<ol id="_755">

4453<li>

4454In a phase III trial, 371 patients were randomly assigned in a 2:1 ratio to receive either gilteritinib or preselected salvage chemotherapy (MEC, FLAG-Ida, azacitidine, or low-dose cytarabine).[<a href="#cit/section_6.16">

445516</a>

4456,<a href="#cit/section_6.17">

445717</a>

4458]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4459<ul id="_756">

4460<li>

4461With a median follow-up of 37.1 months, the median overall survival (OS) was 9.3 months for patients who received gilteritinib versus 5.6 months for patients who received chemotherapy (hazard ratio [HR] for death, 0.665; 95% confidence interval [CI], 0.52&#8211;0.85). The estimated OS rate at 2 years was 20.6% (95% CI, 15.8%&#8211;26.0%) for patients who received gilteritinib and 14.2% (95% CI, 8.3%&#8211;21.6%) for patients who received chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_6.16">

446216</a>

4463] Among those treated with gilteritinib, the median duration of complete response or complete response with partial hematologic recovery was 10 months (interquartile range [IQR], 2.08&#8211;not evaluable), and 23 months (IQR, 4.9&#8211;not evaluable) for just those achieving a complete response.[<a href="#cit/section_6.17">

446417</a>

4465] </li>

4466<li>

4467The rates of complete response and complete response with partial hematologic recovery were higher in patients who received gilteritinib than in patients who received chemotherapy (34% vs. 15.3%; HR, 18.6; 95% CI, 9.8&#8211;27.4). </li>

4468<li>

4469Adverse events of grade 3 or higher were less common in patients who received gilteritinib when adjusted for exposure time.[<a href="#cit/section_6.16">

447016</a>

4471][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4472Level of evidence A1</a>

4473] The most common adverse event of interest was increased liver transaminases for patients who received gilteritinib therapy. If liver transaminase levels (considered related to treatment) increase to more than 5 times the upper limit of normal, gilteritinib therapy is paused. When the enzymes return to less than 2.5 times the upper limit of normal, therapy can resume at a reduced dose of 80 mg once daily.[<a href="#cit/section_6.17">

447417</a>

4475][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4476Level of evidence A1</a>

4477]</li>

4478</ul>

4479</div>

4480</li>

4481</ol>

4482</div>

4483</section>

4484<section id="_757">

4485<h5 id="_757_toc">

4486Enasidenib</h5>

4487<p id="_758" tabindex="-1">

4488Enasidenib is an oral small molecule inhibitor with activity against the mutant IDH2 enzyme.</p>

4489<p id="_759" tabindex="-1">

4490Evidence (enasidenib):</p>

4491<div class="pdq-content-list">

4492<ol id="_760">

4493<li>

4494In a phase I/II study, 214 patients with relapsed or refractory AML were treated with enasidenib.[<a href="#cit/section_6.18">

449518</a>

4496]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4497<ul id="_761">

4498<li>

4499The overall response rate was 40.3% (95% CI, 33.0%&#8211;48.0%), with a median response duration of 5.8 months. </li>

4500<li>

4501This included 46 patients (26.1%) with a CR or a CR with incomplete hematologic recovery. </li>

4502<li>

4503Grade 3 or 4 treatment-related adverse events included indirect hyperbilirubinemia (12%) and differentiation syndrome (7%). As a result, the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) added a <a href="https://www.accessdata.fda.gov/drugsatfda_docs/label/2017/209606s000lbl.pdf" title="https://www.accessdata.fda.gov/drugsatfda_docs/label/2017/209606s000lbl.pdf">

4504boxed warning</a>

4505 to enasidenib, which alerts prescribers that differentiation syndrome can occur.[<a href="#cit/section_6.18">

450618</a>

4507][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4508Level of evidence C3</a>

4509]</li>

4510</ul>

4511</div>

4512</li>

4513</ol>

4514</div>

4515</section>

4516<section id="_762">

4517<h5 id="_762_toc">

4518Ivosidenib</h5>

4519<p id="_763" tabindex="-1">

4520Ivosidenib is an oral small molecule inhibitor with activity against the mutant IDH1 enzyme.</p>

4521<p id="_764" tabindex="-1">

4522Evidence (ivosidenib):</p>

4523<div class="pdq-content-list">

4524<ol id="_765">

4525<li>

4526In a phase I/II study, 179 patients with relapsed or refractory AML were treated with ivosidenib.[<a href="#cit/section_6.19">

452719</a>

4528]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4529<ul id="_766">

4530<li>

4531The overall response rate was 39.1% (95% CI, 31.9%&#8211;46.7%) with a median duration response of 6.5 months (range, 4.6&#8211;9.3). This included 54 patients (30.2%) with a CR or a CR with incomplete hematologic recovery.</li>

4532<li>

4533Over one-third of patients who initially required transfusions became transfusion independent. </li>

4534<li>

4535Grade 3 or higher prolongation of the QT interval was seen in 14 patients (7.8%), and grade 3 or higher differentiation was seen in 7 patients (3.9%). The FDA added a <a href="https://www.accessdata.fda.gov/drugsatfda_docs/label/2019/211192s001lbl.pdf" title="https://www.accessdata.fda.gov/drugsatfda_docs/label/2019/211192s001lbl.pdf">

4536boxed warning</a>

4537 to ivosidenib, which alerts prescribers that differentiation syndrome can occur.[<a href="#cit/section_6.19">

453819</a>

4539][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4540Level of evidence C3</a>

4541]</li>

4542</ul>

4543</div>

4544</li>

4545</ol>

4546</div>

4547</section>

4548<section id="_767">

4549<h5 id="_767_toc">

4550Hypomethylating agents</h5>

4551<p id="_768" tabindex="-1">

4552Evidence (hypomethylating agents):</p>

4553<div class="pdq-content-list">

4554<ol id="_769">

4555<li>

4556In a retrospective analysis, 655 patients with relapsed or primary treatment-refractory AML received either azacitidine (57%) or decitabine (43%).[<a href="#cit/section_6.20">

455720</a>

4558]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4559<ul id="_770">

4560<li>

4561Overall, 16% of patients achieved a CR or a CR with incomplete hematologic recovery and experienced a median OS of 21 months.[<a href="#cit/section_6.20">

456220</a>

4563][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4564Level of evidence C3</a>

4565]</li>

4566</ul>

4567</div>

4568</li>

4569</ol>

4570</div>

4571</section>

4572<section id="_771">

4573<h5 id="_771_toc">

4574Gemtuzumab ozogamicin</h5>

4575<p id="_783" tabindex="-1">

4576The antibody-targeted chemotherapy agent gemtuzumab ozogamicin has been evaluated in patients who had relapsed AML and expressed CD33. </p>

4577<p id="_772" tabindex="-1">

4578Evidence (gemtuzumab ozogamicin):</p>

4579<div class="pdq-content-list">

4580<ol id="_774">

4581<li>

4582A pooled analysis of three open-label, single-arm, phase II studies included 277 patients.[<a href="#cit/section_6.21">

458321</a>

4584]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4585<ul id="_775">

4586<li>

4587The overall response rate was 26%. Thirty-five patients (13%) achieved a CR and 36 patients (13%) achieved a CR without platelet recovery. It is unclear whether the inadequate platelet

4588recovery was the result of megakaryocyte toxic effects of gemtuzumab or subclinical

4589residual leukemia. [<a href="#cit/section_6.21">

459021</a>

4591]</li>

4592</ul>

4593</div>

4594</li>

4595</ol>

4596</div>

4597<p id="_776" tabindex="-1">

4598The long-term outcomes of patients who receive gemtuzumab and achieve CR without platelet recovery

4599are unclear. Gemtuzumab induces profound bone

4600marrow aplasia similar to leukemia induction chemotherapy and also has

4601substantial hepatic toxic effects, including hepatic veno-occlusive

4602disease.[<a href="#cit/section_6.21">

460321</a>

4604][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4605Level of evidence C3</a>

4606]</p>

4607</section>

4608<section id="_777">

4609<h5 id="_777_toc">

4610Clofarabine with or without cytarabine</h5>

4611<p id="_778" tabindex="-1">

4612Evidence (clofarabine with or without cytarabine):</p>

4613<div class="pdq-content-list">

4614<ol id="_779">

4615<li>

4616Clofarabine, a purine nucleoside analogue, was studied as a single agent in 62 patients with relapsed or refractory AML.[<a href="#cit/section_6.22">

461722</a>

4618]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4619<ul id="_780">

4620<li>

4621Eight of 19 patients who received treatment for their first relapse experienced a complete response.</li>

4622</ul>

4623</div>

4624 </li>

4625<li>

4626Clofarabine was administered in combination with intermediate-dose cytarabine in patients with relapsed or refractory AML.[<a href="#cit/section_6.23">

462723</a>

4628]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4629<ul id="_781">

4630<li>

4631Seven of 29 patients with AML or myelodysplastic syndrome who received treatment for their first relapse experienced a CR.[<a href="#cit/section_6.23">

463223</a>

4633][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4634Level of evidence C3</a>

4635]</li>

4636</ul>

4637</div>

4638</li>

4639</ol>

4640</div>

4641</section>

4642</section>

4643</section>

4644<section id="_560">

4645<h3 id="_560_toc">

4646Allogeneic Hematopoietic Cell Transplantation</h3>

4647<p id="_84" tabindex="-1">

4648When patients with relapsed disease are treated aggressively, they may have extended

4649disease-free survival (DFS); however, patients with relapsed disease can only be cured with HCT.[<a href="#cit/section_6.24">

465024</a>

4651][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4652Level of evidence C2</a>

4653] Allogeneic HCT for patients in their second

4654CR provides better DFS rates than transplantation for patients in relapse.[<a href="#cit/section_6.25">

465525</a>

4656][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4657Level of evidence C1</a>

4658] </p>

4659<p id="_561" tabindex="-1">

4660Evidence (allogeneic HCT):</p>

4661<div class="pdq-content-list">

4662<ol id="_562">

4663<li>

4664 Current transplant outcomes are reported by the Center for International Blood and Marrow Transplantation Registry. The group reported the following outcomes for transplants done in the United States between 2008 and 2018:[<a href="#cit/section_6.26">

466526</a>

4666][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4667Level of evidence C2</a>

4668]<div class="pdq-content-list">

4669<ul id="_716">

4670<li>

4671 The 3-year survival rate was 53% for patients with AML in second or subsequent CR versus 31% for patients with relapsed disease (or never in a CR) who underwent a matched sibling donor transplant.</li>

4672<li>

4673The 3-year survival rate was 50% for patients with AML in second or subsequent CR versus 30% for patients with relapsed disease (or who never achieved CR) who underwent a matched unrelated donor transplant.</li>

4674</ul>

4675</div>

4676</li>

4677</ol>

4678</div>

4679<p id="_85" tabindex="-1">

4680Allogeneic HCT can

4681be effective salvage therapy in some patients whose disease fails to go into remission with intensive

4682chemotherapy (primary refractory leukemia). A number of retrospective studies have demonstrated the ability of allogeneic HCT to induce remission in primary refractory disease.[<a href="#cit/section_6.27">

468327</a>

4684]</p>

4685<p id="_721" tabindex="-1">

4686Evidence (allogeneic HCT to induce remission):</p>

4687<div class="pdq-content-list">

4688<ol id="_722">

4689<li>

4690 In one retrospective analysis of 168 patients with AML and primary refractory disease who underwent allogeneic HCT, the 5-year OS rate was 22%.[<a href="#cit/section_6.28">

469128</a>

4692] </li>

4693<li>

4694Another analysis was conducted among patients enrolled in a prospective cooperative group trial, <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00085709">

4695SWOG S0106</a>

4696 (NCT00085709).[<a href="#cit/section_6.29">

469729</a>

4698] <div class="pdq-content-list">

4699<ul id="_723">

4700<li>

4701Of the 589 patients treated in the cooperative group trial, 150 (25%) had primary refractory disease.</li>

4702<li>

4703Among the 64 patients with primary refractory disease who received an allogeneic HCT, the 4-year survival rate was 48% compared with 4% among the 86 patients who did not undergo transplantation.[<a href="#cit/section_6.29">

470429</a>

4705][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810039&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4706Level of evidence C3</a>

4707]</li>

4708</ul>

4709</div>

4710</li>

4711</ol>

4712</div>

4713<p id="_724" tabindex="-1">

4714Randomized trials testing the efficacy of this approach are not available. </p>

4715</section>

4716<section id="_TrialSearch_80_sid_6">

4717<h3 id="_TrialSearch_80_sid_6_toc">

4718Current Clinical Trials</h3>

4719<p id="_TrialSearch_80_22" tabindex="-1">

4720Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

4721advanced clinical trial search</a>

4722 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

4723General information</a>

4724 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

4775[PUBMED Abstract]</a>

4776</li>
