4851

4852 <section id="_355">

4853

4854 <h2>

4855Treatment of Acute Promyelocytic Leukemia (APL)</h2>

4856

4857 <div id="_section_355" class="pdq-sections">

4858<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

4859<h6>

4860In This Section</h6>

4861<ul>

4862<li>

4863<a href="#_690_toc">

4864Treatment of Newly Diagnosed APL<ul>

4865<li>

4866<a href="#_673_toc">

4867ATRA plus ATO for low- to intermediate-risk disease</a>

4868</li>

4869<li>

4870<a href="#_682_toc">

4871ATRA plus chemotherapy, followed by ATO-based consolidation therapy for high-risk disease</a>

4872</li>

4873</ul>

4874</a>

4875</li>

4876<li>

4877<a href="#_693_toc">

4878Treatment of Recurrent APL<ul>

4879<li>

4880<a href="#_696_toc">

4881ATO with or without chemotherapy</a>

4882</li>

4883<li>

4884<a href="#_699_toc">

4885HCT</a>

4886</li>

4887</ul>

4888</a>

4889</li>

4890<li>

4891<a href="#_TrialSearch_355_sid_7_toc">

4892Current Clinical Trials</a>

4893</li>

4894</ul>

4895</nav>

4896<p id="_518" tabindex="-1">

4897Special consideration must be given to induction therapy for APL. Treatment is centered around the use of differentiating agents to clear the leukemic cells. Early mortality is related to bleeding, differentiation syndrome, or infection. High complete remission (CR) rates are very common across treatment regimens, and persistent disease or relapse is rare.</p>

4898<section id="_690">

4899<h3 id="_690_toc">

4900Treatment of Newly Diagnosed APL</h3>

4901<p id="_691" tabindex="-1">

4902Treatment options for newly diagnosed APL include the following:</p>

4903<div class="pdq-content-list">

4904<ol id="_408">

4905<li>

4906 <a href="/types/leukemia/hp/adult-aml-treatment-pdq#_673">

4907All-trans retinoic acid (ATRA) plus arsenic trioxide (ATO) for low- to intermediate-risk disease</a>

4908.</li>

4909<li>

4910<a href="/types/leukemia/hp/adult-aml-treatment-pdq#_682">

4911 ATRA plus chemotherapy, followed by ATO-based consolidation therapy for high-risk disease</a>

4912.</li>

4913</ol>

4914</div>

4915<p id="_519" tabindex="-1">

4916ATRA induces terminal differentiation of the

4917leukemic cells followed by restoration of nonclonal hematopoiesis.

4918Administration of ATRA leads to rapid resolution of coagulopathy in most patients, and heparin administration is not required in patients

4919receiving ATRA. However, randomized trials have not shown a reduction in

4920morbidity and mortality during ATRA induction when compared with chemotherapy.

4921ATRA administration may result in the following conditions:</p>

4922<div class="pdq-content-list">

4923<ul id="_520">

4924<li>

4925<strong>

4926Differentiation syndrome:</strong>

4927 Administration of ATRA can lead to a syndrome of

4928respiratory distress, known as differentiation syndrome. Prompt

4929recognition of the syndrome and aggressive administration of steroids can

4930prevent severe respiratory distress.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

49311</a>

4932]</li>

4933<li>

4934<strong>

4935Hyperleukocytosis:</strong>

4936 The optimal management of

4937ATRA-induced hyperleukocytosis has not been established. Hyperleukocytosis in APL is typically treated with the addition of cytotoxic chemotherapy. Leukopheresis is not recommended because of an increased risk of complications such as bleeding events and disseminated intravascular coagulation.</li>

4938</ul>

4939</div>

4940<p id="_403" tabindex="-1">

4941Studies performed in the 1990s demonstrated that overall survival (OS) rates improved in patients receiving ATRA in addition to chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

49422</a>

4943,<a href="#cit/section_7.3">

49443</a>

4945] ATO, an agent with both differentiation-inducing and apoptosis-inducing

4946properties against APL cells, is also used in the treatment of APL. Induction remission therapy for APL is determined by disease risk. Low- to intermediate-risk APL (white blood cell [WBC] count &#8804;10 x10<span class="sup">

49479</span>

4948/L) is treated without chemotherapy (ATRA and ATO), and high-risk is treated with a combination of ATRA and ATO plus chemotherapy.</p>

4949<section id="_673">

4950<h4 id="_673_toc">

4951ATRA plus ATO for low- to intermediate-risk disease</h4>

4952<p id="_674" tabindex="-1">

4953Evidence (ATRA plus ATO for low- to intermediate-risk disease):</p>

4954<div class="pdq-content-list">

4955<ol id="_680">

4956<li>

4957 In a phase III, randomized controlled, multicenter trial in patients with APL classified as low-to-intermediate risk (WBC count, &#8804;10&#215;10<span class="sup">

49589</span>

4959/L) ATRA plus chemotherapy was compared with ATRA plus ATO.[<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

49604</a>

4961] <div class="pdq-content-list">

4962<ul id="_681">

4963<li>

4964 CR rates were equally high for both groups. CR occurred in all 77 patients (100%) who could be evaluated in the ATRA plus ATO group and in 75 of 79 patients (95%) in the ATRA plus chemotherapy group (<em>

4965P</em>

4966 = .12).</li>

4967<li>

4968 With a median follow-up of 34.4 months, the 2-year OS rate was 99% (95% confidence interval [CI], 96%&#8722;100%) in the ATRA plus ATO group, and 91% (95% CI, 85%&#8722;97%) in the ATRA plus chemotherapy group (<em>

4969P</em>

4970 = .02).</li>

4971<li>

4972 The 2-year cumulative incidence of relapse was similarly low in both groups, 1% (95% CI, 0%&#8722;4%) in the ATRA plus ATO group and 6% (95% CI, 0%&#8722;11%) in the ATRA plus chemotherapy group (<em>

4973P</em>

4974 = .24).</li>

4975<li>

4976 The primary end point was event-free survival (EFS) (defined as no achievement of hematologic CR after induction therapy, no achievement of molecular CR after three consolidation courses, molecular relapse, hematologic relapse, or death). The 2-year EFS rate was 97% for the ATRA plus ATO group and 85% in the ATRA plus chemotherapy group (<em>

4977P</em>

4978 &lt; .001 for noninferiority).</li>

4979</ul>

4980</div>

4981</li>

4982<li>

4983The results of this chemotherapy-free regimen for low- to intermediate-risk APL were confirmed in a second, phase III, randomized controlled trial.[<a href="#cit/section_7.5">

49845</a>

4985][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810017&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4986Level of evidence A1</a>

4987]</li>

4988</ol>

4989</div>

4990</section>

4991<section id="_682">

4992<h4 id="_682_toc">

4993ATRA plus chemotherapy, followed by ATO-based consolidation therapy for high-risk disease</h4>

4994<p id="_683" tabindex="-1">

4995Remission induction with a combination of anthracycline and ATRA is used for remission induction in patients with high-risk disease (WBC count, &gt;10x10<span class="sup">

49969</span>

4997/L).</p>

4998<p id="_684" tabindex="-1">

4999Evidence (ATRA plus chemotherapy, followed by ATO-based consolidation therapy for high-risk disease):</p>

5000<div class="pdq-content-list">

5001<ol id="_685">

5002<li>

5003The <a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT00180128">

5004AIDA-2000</a>

5005 study (NCT00180128) combined oral ATRA until CR or for a maximum of 45 days and four doses of intravenous idarubicin (12 mg/m<span class="sup">

50062</span>

5007) on days 2, 4, 6, and 8. Consolidation was then risk stratified so low- to intermediate-risk patients received additional cycles of anthracycline and ATRA, and high-risk patients also received cytarabine, etoposide, 6-thioguanine, and CHT chemotherapy (6-mercaptopurine plus methotrexate) as consolidation.[<a href="#cit/section_7.6">

50086</a>

5009]<div class="pdq-content-list">

5010<ul id="_686">

5011<li>

5012 After induction, 420 of 445 patients (94.4%) treated on the AIDA-2000 protocol were in CR. The 6-year OS rate was 87.4% and the cumulative incidence of relapse rate was 10.7%.[<a href="#cit/section_7.6">

50136</a>

5014][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5015Level of evidence B4</a>

5016] </li>

5017</ul>

5018</div>

5019</li>

5020<li>

5021 In the phase II APML4 study, ATO was added to the ATRA-and-idarubicin remission&#8722;induction backbone.[<a href="#cit/section_7.7">

50227</a>

5023] <div class="pdq-content-list">

5024<ul id="_687">

5025<li>

5026 Of the 124 patients who could be evaluated, there were 4 (3.2%) early deaths and 118 (95%) hematologic CRs.</li>

5027<li>

5028 The 2-year freedom-from-relapse rate was 97.5% (95% CI, 90.4%&#8722;99.4%), the failure-free survival rate was 88.1% (95% CI, 80.7%&#8722;92.8%), and the OS rate was 93.2% (95% CI, 85.8%&#8722;96.8%).[<a href="#cit/section_7.7">

50297</a>

5030][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5031Level of evidence B4</a>

5032]</li>

5033</ul>

5034</div>

5035<p id="_688" tabindex="-1">

5036An ATO-based regimen, which includes gemtuzumab ozogamicin as the only cytotoxic drug, has been developed.</p>

5037</li>

5038<li>

5039In a single-institution study, patients received ATRA plus ATO induction. They also received a dose of gemtuzumab ozogamicin (or idarubicin) if the WBC was greater than 10 x 10<span class="sup">

50409</span>

5041/L on presentation or rose to more than 30 x 10<span class="sup">

50429</span>

5043/L during induction.[<a href="#cit/section_7.8">

50448</a>

5045] Patients in remission received ATO and ATRA in alternating months for a total of seven cycles as consolidation; gemtuzumab ozogamicin was substituted if either ATO or ATRA were discontinued because of toxicity. <div class="pdq-content-list">

5046<ul id="_689">

5047<li>

5048 Of the 54 patients with high-risk disease treated on the protocol, one patient received both gemtuzumab ozogamicin and idarubicin (12 mg/m<span class="sup">

50492</span>

5050 daily for 3 days) because of persistent leukocytosis despite receiving gemtuzumab ozogamicin.</li>

5051<li>

5052The CR rate was 96%, and five (9%) patients relapsed.</li>

5053<li>

5054 The 5-year rates were 81% for EFS, 89% for disease-free survival (DFS), and 86% for OS, indicating that the responses are durable.</li>

5055<li>

5056 Across the entire study population, the 5-year OS rate was similar among the 45 high-risk patients who received gemtuzumab ozogamicin (84%) compared with the seven patients who received a dose of idarubicin (100%, <em>

5057P</em>

5058 = .453).[<a href="#cit/section_7.8">

50598</a>

5060][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810033&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

5061Level of evidence B4</a>

5062]</li>

5063</ul>

5064</div>

5065<p id="_692" tabindex="-1">

5066Long-term follow up from this study has been published.[<a href="#cit/section_7.9">

50679</a>

5068] </p>

5069</li>

5070</ol>

5071</div>

5072</section>

5073<p id="_679" tabindex="-1">

5074It is important to note that most current regimens for the treatment of APL include some form of maintenance therapy. A meta-analysis of randomized trials has indicated that maintenance clearly improves DFS but not OS; however, these trials did not include ATO-containing regimens.</p>

5075</section>

5076<section id="_693">

5077<h3 id="_693_toc">

5078Treatment of Recurrent APL</h3>

5079<p id="_694" tabindex="-1">

5080Treatment options for recurrent APL include the following:</p>

5081<div class="pdq-content-list">

5082<ol id="_695">

5083<li>

5084<a href="/types/leukemia/hp/adult-aml-treatment-pdq#_696">

5085ATO with or without chemotherapy</a>

5086.</li>

5087<li>

5088<a href="/types/leukemia/hp/adult-aml-treatment-pdq#_699">

5089Hematopoietic cell transplantation (HCT)</a>

5090.</li>

5091</ol>

5092</div>

5093<section id="_696">

5094<h4 id="_696_toc">

5095ATO with or without chemotherapy</h4>

5096<p id="_86" tabindex="-1">

5097ATO has high rates of second remission in patients with relapsed APL.[<a href="#cit/section_7.10">

509810</a>

5099] As a single agent, ATO can lead to complete response rates of 80% to 90% in patients with hematologic relapse, and 70% to 80% in patients with molecular remission.[<a href="#cit/section_7.11">

510011</a>

5101-<a href="#cit/section_7.14">

510214</a>

5103] The choice of salvage therapy is based on the previous therapy and interval of time between first remission and relapse. </p>

5104<div class="pdq-content-list">

5105<ul id="_697">

5106<li>

5107 In patients with early relapse less than 6 months after ATRA and ATO, anthracycline-based regimens and ATRA as given for initial remission induction for high-risk disease should be considered.</li>

5108<li>

5109 In patients who relapse less than 6 months after ATRA and anthracycline-based regimens (no previous ATO exposure), ATO-based regimens should be considered.</li>

5110<li>

5111 In all patients with late relapse (&gt;6 months), ATO-based regimens with or without anthracycline or gemtuzumab ozogamicin should be considered.

5112</li>

5113</ul>

5114</div>

5115<p id="_698" tabindex="-1">

5116For patients receiving ATO as salvage therapy, a small randomized trial suggested that the addition of ATRA does not confer any benefit over ATO alone in patients who previously received ATRA.[<a href="#cit/section_7.14">

511714</a>

5118] In this 20-patient study, the complete response rate after one cycle of ATO with or without ATRA was 80%.</p>

5119</section>

5120<section id="_699">

5121<h4 id="_699_toc">

5122HCT</h4>

5123<p id="_700" tabindex="-1">

5124Some patients in second remission with ATO have experienced long-term DFS after autologous stem cell transplantation,[<a href="#cit/section_7.15">

512515</a>

5126,<a href="#cit/section_7.16">

512716</a>

5128] and it can be considered in patients who are in molecular remission (negative quantitative polymerase chain reaction [PCR] on a marrow sample). Patients who do not go into remission or have evidence of minimal residual disease by quantitative PCR on a marrow sample after salvage therapy are considered for an allogeneic HCT.[<a href="#cit/section_7.17">

512917</a>

5130] A registry study reported a 3-year OS rate after transplant in second CR of 80% compared with 59% in patients without transplant (<em>

5131P</em>

5132 = .03).[<a href="#cit/section_7.10">

513310</a>

5134] </p>

5135</section>

5136</section>

5137<section id="_TrialSearch_355_sid_7">

5138<h3 id="_TrialSearch_355_sid_7_toc">

5139Current Clinical Trials</h3>

5140<p id="_TrialSearch_355_22" tabindex="-1">

5141Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

5142advanced clinical trial search</a>

5143 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

5144General information</a>

5145 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

5146</section>

5265 <section id="_AboutThis_1">

5266

5267 <h2>

5268About This PDQ Summary</h2>

5269

5270 <div id="_section_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

5271<section id="_AboutThis_2">

5272<h3 id="_AboutThis_2_toc">

5273Purpose of This Summary</h3>

5274<p id="_AboutThis_3" tabindex="-1">

5275This PDQ cancer information summary for health professionals provides comprehensive, peer-reviewed, evidence-based information about the treatment of acute myeloid leukemia. It is intended as a resource to inform and assist clinicians in the care of their patients. It does not provide formal guidelines or recommendations for making health care decisions.</p>

5276</section>

5277<section id="_AboutThis_4">

5278<h3 id="_AboutThis_4_toc">

5279Reviewers and Updates</h3>

5280<p id="_AboutThis_5" tabindex="-1">

5281This summary is reviewed regularly and updated as necessary by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment">

5282PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board</a>

5283, which is editorially independent of the National Cancer Institute (NCI). The summary reflects an independent review of the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or the National Institutes of Health (NIH).</p>

5284<p id="_AboutThis_22" tabindex="-1">

5285 Board members review recently published articles each month to determine whether an article should:</p>

5286<div class="pdq-content-list">

5287<ul id="_AboutThis_6">

5288<li>

5289be discussed at a meeting,</li>

5290<li>

5291be cited with text, or</li>

5292<li>

5293replace or update an existing article that is already cited.</li>

5294</ul>

5295</div>

5296<p id="_AboutThis_7" tabindex="-1">

5297Changes to the summaries are made through a consensus process in which Board members evaluate the strength of the evidence in the published articles and determine how the article should be included in the summary.</p>

5298<p id="" tabindex="-1">

5299The lead reviewer for Acute Myeloid Leukemia Treatment is:</p>

5300<div class="pdq-content-list">

5301<ul id="">

5302<li>

5303Aaron Gerds, MD</li>

5304</ul>

5305</div>

5306<p id="_AboutThis_9" tabindex="-1">

5307Any comments or questions about the summary content should be submitted to Cancer.gov through the NCI website's <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us" title="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us">

5308Email Us</a>

5309. Do not contact the individual Board Members with questions or comments about the summaries. Board members will not respond to individual inquiries.</p>

5310</section>

5311<section id="_AboutThis_10">

5312<h3 id="_AboutThis_10_toc">

5313Levels of Evidence</h3>

5314<p id="_AboutThis_11" tabindex="-1">

5315Some of the reference citations in this summary are accompanied by a level-of-evidence designation. These designations are intended to help readers assess the strength of the evidence supporting the use of specific interventions or approaches. The PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board uses a <a href="/publications/pdq/levels-evidence/treatment">

5316formal evidence ranking system</a>

5317 in developing its level-of-evidence designations.</p>

5318</section>

Although the content of PDQ documents can be used freely as text, it cannot be identified as an NCI PDQ cancer information summary unless it is presented in its entirety and is regularly updated. However, an author would be permitted to write a sentence such as &#8220;NCI&#8217;s PDQ cancer information summary about breast cancer prevention states the risks succinctly: [include excerpt from the summary].&#8221;</p>
